<p>Borrowed from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_language" class="extiw" title="w:French language">French</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="fr"><a href = vnd.unilang:champignon.html>champignon</a></i>.

<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:champignon.html>champignon</a></strong> <span class="gender"><abbr title="masculine gender">m</abbr></span> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl p-form-of" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:champignons.html>champignons</a></b>, <i>diminutive</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl diminutive-form-of" lang="nl"><a href = vnd.unilang:champignon.html>champignonnetje</a></b> <span class="gender"><abbr title="neuter gender">n</abbr></span>)
</p>

***chaser.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:chaser.html>chaser</a> (52214)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_1">Etymology 1</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_English" class="extiw" title="w:Middle English">Middle English</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="enm"><a href = vnd.unilang:chaser.html>chaser</a></i>, <i class="Latn mention" lang="enm">chacer</i>, <i class="Latn mention" lang="enm">chasour</i>, borrowed from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_French" class="extiw" title="w:Old French">Old French</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="fro">chaceür</i>, <i class="Latn mention" lang="fro">chaceor</i>, from <i class="Latn mention" lang="fro">chacier</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">to chase, hunt</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>; <a href = vnd.unilang:later.html>later</a> senses from or influenced by <i class="Latn mention" lang="en">chase</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">pursue</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span> + |  <i class="Latn mention" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:dictatoriaal.html>-er</a></i>. Doublet of <i class="Latn mention" lang="en">chasseur</i>.
</p>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:chaser.html>chaser</a></strong> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en p-form-of" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:chasers.html>chasers</a></b>)
</p>
<ol><li>A person or thing (ship, plane, car, etc.) that chases. <span class="defdate">[from 14th c.]</span>
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2007</b>,  David Oatman,  <cite>Old Favorites, New Fun</cite>, page 32:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">One student <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> the <b><a href = vnd.unilang:chaser.html>chaser</a></b> and the other <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> the chasee. Give the chasee three <a href = vnd.unilang:seconds.html>seconds</a> to get away and then allow the <a href = vnd.unilang:chaser.html>chaser</a> to attempt to tag the chasee.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">archaic</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> A hunter. <span class="defdate">[from 15th c.]</span></li>
<li>A person who does the chasing on metalwork.</li>
<li>A horse: <span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">originally</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> a horse used for hunting; <span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">now</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> a horse trained for steeplechasing, a steeplechaser. <span class="defdate">[from 14th c.]</span>
<ul><li><b>2002</b>, <a href = vnd.unilang:nick.html>Nick</a> Mordin, <i>Betting for a Living</i>, page 351:
<dl><dd>"[I]<a href = vnd.unilang:t.html>t</a> looked like The Fellow <a href = vnd.unilang:was.html>was</a> the <a href = vnd.unilang:best.html>best</a> steeplechaser in many years. He'd earned the <a href = vnd.unilang:best.html>best</a> speed rating I'd ever given a <b><a href = vnd.unilang:chaser.html>chaser</a></b>."</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>2003</b>, Avalyn Hunter, <i>American Classic Pedigrees 1914-2002</i>, page 458:
<dl><dd>"Wild Risk...<a href = vnd.unilang:had.html>had</a> his greatest successes as a steeplechaser rather than a <a href = vnd.unilang:flat.html>flat</a> racer... It <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:rare.html>rare</a> indeed that a '<b><a href = vnd.unilang:chaser.html>chaser</a></b> <a href = vnd.unilang:halal.html>-</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:even.html>even</a> one as good as wild risk <a href = vnd.unilang:halal.html>-</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:makes.html>makes</a> a good <a href = vnd.unilang:flat.html>flat</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:sire.html>sire</a>."</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>2004</b>, <i>Sports Ticket: Live the Action!</i> by Sportsfile, page 179:
<dl><dd>"<a href = vnd.unilang:oh.html>Oh</a>, that final <a href = vnd.unilang:furlong.html>furlong</a>! It can be both agony and ecstasy. Anyone who doubts that should have seen the television close-up of <a href = vnd.unilang:jim.html>Jim</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:lewis.html>Lewis</a> as his great <b><a href = vnd.unilang:chaser.html>chaser</a></b> <a href = vnd.unilang:best.html>Best</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:mate.html>Mate</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:came.html>came</a> up the final hill at Cheltenham in 2004 to clich a hat-trick of Gold <a href = vnd.unilang:cups.html>Cups</a>. ... <a href = vnd.unilang:best.html>Best</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:mate.html>mate</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> the <a href = vnd.unilang:best.html>best</a> steeplechaser <a href = vnd.unilang:we.html>we</a> have seen for years and all being well will be at the Cheltenham Festival again in 2005 to try and make it four Gold <a href = vnd.unilang:cups.html>Cups</a>."</dd></dl></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Britain" class="extiw" title="w:Great Britain">Britain</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> A strong alcoholic <a href = vnd.unilang:drink.html>drink</a> (such as a spirit) that <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> drunk after a weaker alcoholic <a href = vnd.unilang:drink.html>drink</a>.</li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States" class="extiw" title="w:United States">US</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> A mild <a href = vnd.unilang:drink.html>drink</a> consumed immediately after a <a href = vnd.unilang:drink.html>drink</a> of hard liquor. <span class="defdate">[from 19th c.]</span>
<ul><li><b>1947</b>, John Clarkson <a href = vnd.unilang:jay.html>Jay</a>, <i>Skiing the Americas</i>, page <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=8QeCAAAAMAAJamp;q=%22straight%2C+no+chaser%22amp;pgis=1search_anchor">115</a>:
<dl><dd>"<a href = vnd.unilang:cowboys.html>Cowboys</a> in high-heeled boots teeter along its sidewalks, or push the <a href = vnd.unilang:swinging.html>swinging</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:doors.html>doors</a> aside for a shot or two — straight, no <b><a href = vnd.unilang:chaser.html>chaser</a></b>."</dd></dl></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">logging<span class="ib-comma">,</span> obsolete</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> Someone that follows <a href = vnd.unilang:logs.html>logs</a> out of the forest in order to signal a yarder engineer to <a href = vnd.unilang:stop.html>stop</a> them if they become fouled <span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content qualifier-content">also called a <a href = vnd.unilang:frogger.html>frogger</a></span><span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">)</span>.
<ul><li><b>1900</b>, <i>Pamphlets on Logging Equipment</i> (author unknown), page 22:
<dl><dd>"...on one end known as a Bardon choker hook, to facilitate making a <a href = vnd.unilang:loop.html>loop</a>. It stays tight and <a href = vnd.unilang:makes.html>makes</a> it unnecessary for the "<b><a href = vnd.unilang:chaser.html>chaser</a></b>" or "choker <a href = vnd.unilang:setter.html>setter</a>" to follow the "turn" to the landing as might have to be done if <a href = vnd.unilang:tongs.html>tongs</a> are used"</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>1913</b>, <a href = vnd.unilang:ralph.html>Ralph</a> Clement Bryant, <i>Logging: The Principles and General Methods of Operation in the United States</i>, page 219:
<dl><dd>"A <b><a href = vnd.unilang:chaser.html>chaser</a></b> follows the <a href = vnd.unilang:logs.html>logs</a> to the landing, often riding in a rigging sled hollowed out of a log, which <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> attached to the rear log. The <b><a href = vnd.unilang:chaser.html>chaser</a></b> can signal to the road engineer at any point..."</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>1918</b>, <i>United States Shipping Board Emergency Fleet Corporation: Hearing Before the Committee on Commerce</i>:
<dl><dd>"and the <b><a href = vnd.unilang:chaser.html>chaser</a></b> <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> the fellow whose job it <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> to follow along after these <a href = vnd.unilang:logs.html>logs</a> to..."</dd></dl></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">logging</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> One who unhooks chokers from the <a href = vnd.unilang:logs.html>logs</a> at the landing.
<ul><li><b>1956</b>, Stewart Hall Holbrook, <i>Holy Old Mackinaw: A Natural History of the American Lumber-Jack</i>, page 184:
<dl><dd>"The <i>rigging <a href = vnd.unilang:slinger.html>slinger</a></i> <a href = vnd.unilang:hooks.html>hooks</a> the chokers to the main line, the <i><a href = vnd.unilang:chaser.html>chaser</a></i> unhooks them at the spar tree."</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>1975</b>, <a href = vnd.unilang:fred.html>Fred</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:moira.html>Moira</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:farrow.html>Farrow</a>, <i>Nobody Here But Us: <a href = vnd.unilang:pioneers.html>Pioneers</a> of the North</i>, page 170:
<dl><dd><i>A <a href = vnd.unilang:chaser.html>chaser</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:was.html>was</a> the <a href = vnd.unilang:man.html>man</a> who unhooked the <a href = vnd.unilang:logs.html>logs</a> that <a href = vnd.unilang:were.html>were</a> yarded in to the spar tree.</i></dd></dl></li>
<li><b>1985</b>, John Kenneth Pearce, George Stenzel, <i>Logging and Pulpwood Production</i> pages 242-243:
<dl><dd>"When the turn arrives at the landing, the <b><a href = vnd.unilang:chaser.html>chaser</a></b> directs the engineer where to drop the turn by hand signals. The <b><a href = vnd.unilang:chaser.html>chaser</a></b> then unhooks the chokers, <a href = vnd.unilang:gets.html>gets</a> in the clear, and singlas to reel in the haulback line".</dd></dl></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href = vnd.unilang:slang.html>slang</a><span class="ib-comma">,</span> historical</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> A piece of music, etc. played after a performance while the audience leaves.
<ul><li><b>1969</b>, Robert <a href = vnd.unilang:dean.html>Dean</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:klassen.html>Klassen</a>, <i>The Tent-repertoire Theatre: A Rural American Institution</i> (page 95)
<dl><dd>After the final curtain the orchestra played a "<b><a href = vnd.unilang:chaser.html>chaser</a></b>" which <a href = vnd.unilang:was.html>was</a> music played while the audience members not remaining for the after-show concert left the theatre.</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>2009</b>, <a href = vnd.unilang:andre.html>Andre</a> Gaudreault, <i>American Cinema 1890-1909: Themes and Variations</i> (page 113)
<dl><dd><a href = vnd.unilang:films.html>Films</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:had.html>had</a> become a regular feature of the typical <a href = vnd.unilang:vaudeville.html>vaudeville</a> program, ending most programs and occasionally serving as a “<b><a href = vnd.unilang:chaser.html>chaser</a></b>” that encouraged audiences to leave the continuous programs rather than retain their seats to watch them a second time.</dd></dl></li></ul></li>
<li>One of a series of adjacent light bulbs that cycle on and off to give the illusion of movement.</li>
<li><span class="form-of-definition use-with-mention">Synonym of <span class="form-of-definition-link"><i class="Latn mention" lang="en">prison <a href = vnd.unilang:chaser.html>chaser</a></i></span></span></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href = vnd.unilang:slang.html>slang</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> A person who seeks out sexual <a href = vnd.unilang:partners.html>partners</a> with a particular quality:

<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_2">Etymology 2</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <i class="Latn mention" lang="en">chase</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">groove; decorate metal</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span> + |  <i class="Latn mention" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:dictatoriaal.html>-er</a></i>.
</p>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun_2">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:chaser.html>chaser</a></strong> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en p-form-of" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:chasers.html>chasers</a></b>)
</p>
<ol><li>Someone who chases <span class="gloss-brac">(</span><span class="gloss-content">decorates</span><span class="gloss-brac">)</span> metal; a person who decorates metal by engraving or embossing. <span class="defdate">[from 18th c.]</span>
<ul><li><b>1863</b>, Virginia <a href = vnd.unilang:penny.html>Penny</a>, <i>The Employments of Women: A Cyclopaedia of Woman's Work</i>, page 100:
<dl><dd>"<a href = vnd.unilang:mr.html>Mr</a> B., heraldic <b><a href = vnd.unilang:chaser.html>chaser</a></b>, says there are several processes in making heraldy plates, sketching, engraving, embossing, chasing and burnishing."</dd>
<dd>"H. amp; C., manufacturers of cloth and <a href = vnd.unilang:gilt.html>gilt</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:buttons.html>buttons</a>, say it requires some weeks to learn to chase the <a href = vnd.unilang:gilt.html>gilt</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:buttons.html>buttons</a>, which are done with small metal tools and a hammer. <b><a href = vnd.unilang:chasers.html>Chasers</a></b> are paid by the peice, working ten <a href = vnd.unilang:hours.html>hours</a> a day, and some can earn $1 a day."</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>1971</b>, George <a href = vnd.unilang:bernard.html>Bernard</a> Hughes, <i>Living Crafts</i>, page 36:
<dl><dd>"<a href = vnd.unilang:flat.html>Flat</a> chasing in sunken or low relief <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> a technique by which the ornament <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> formed by beating down the ground from the front. This <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> done in essentially the same manner as repoussé work, where the ornament appears in high relief, but the design <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> punched from the face of the silver plate. ... Sometimes, instead of applying a freehand design, the <b><a href = vnd.unilang:chaser.html>chaser</a></b> <a href = vnd.unilang:covers.html>covers</a> the greased suface with a paper pattern in which the design <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> pricked with <a href = vnd.unilang:pins.html>pins</a>."</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>1972</b>, Richard <a href = vnd.unilang:came.html>Came</a>, <i>Silver</i>, page 7:
<dl><dd>"Chasing in general can be distinguised from engraving, in that the design can be seen on the reverse or inside of the pieces. Having outlined the pattern on the surface, the <b><a href = vnd.unilang:chaser.html>chaser</a></b> <a href = vnd.unilang:cuts.html>cuts</a> and at the same time slightly depresses the surface. A light hammer can be used in this process also."</dd></dl></li></ul></li>
<li>A tool used for cleaning out screw threads, either as an integral part of a tap or <a href = vnd.unilang:die.html>die</a> to remove waste material produced by the cutting tool, or as a separate tool to repair damaged threads. <span class="defdate">[from 19th c.]</span>
<ul><li><b>1894</b>, <i>Machinery</i> (author(s) unknown), page 141:
<dl><dd>"In Fig. i <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> shown one of the <b><a href = vnd.unilang:chasers.html>chasers</a></b> in the position which it occupies in cutting a thread."</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>1918</b>, Franklin Day Jones, <i>Thread-cutting Methods: A Treatise on the Operation and Use of Various Tools and <a href = vnd.unilang:machines.html>Machines</a> for forming screw threads...</i>, page 32:
<dl><dd>"Many screw threads are also finished completely with <b><a href = vnd.unilang:chasers.html>chasers</a></b> of this type, although they are not adapted for extremely acurate work unless the teeth are ground after hardening, because the pitch of the <b><a href = vnd.unilang:chaser.html>chaser</a></b> teeth <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> affected more or less by..."</dd></dl></li>
<li><b>1994</b>, Francis <a href = vnd.unilang:t.html>T</a>. Farago, Mark A. <a href = vnd.unilang:curtis.html>Curtis</a>, <i>Handbook of Dimensional Measurement</i>, page 467:
<dl><dd>"The category of thread cutting tools inlcudes both the single-point and multiple-point [<b><a href = vnd.unilang:chaser.html>chaser</a></b> type] lathe <a href = vnd.unilang:cutters.html>cutters</a>."</dd></dl></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">nautical</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> A chase gun.
<dl><dd><i>bow <b><a href = vnd.unilang:chaser.html>chaser</a></b>; stern <b><a href = vnd.unilang:chaser.html>chaser</a></b></i></dd></dl></li></ol>

***chateaubriand.html
<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:chateaubriand.html>chateaubriand</a> (94648)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>Borrowed from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_language" class="extiw" title="w:French language">French</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="fr"><a href = vnd.unilang:chateaubriand.html>chateaubriand</a></i>, named after French Romantic writer <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois-Ren%C3%A9_de_Chateaubriand" class="extiw" title="w:François-René de Chateaubriand"><span class="Latn" lang="en">François-René <a href = vnd.unilang:de.html>de</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:chateaubriand.html>Chateaubriand</a></span></a>, who <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:said.html>said</a> to have enjoyed this type of <a href = vnd.unilang:steak.html>steak</a>.
</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>

</p>

<head> <meta charset='utf-8'> </head> <body><h1> <a href = vnd.unilang:chatterbox.html>chatterbox</a> (47645)</h1><br><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p><i class="Latn mention" lang="en">chatter</i> + |  <i class="Latn mention" lang="en">box</i>

<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:chatterbox.html>chatterbox</a></strong> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en p-form-of" lang="en">chatterboxes</b>)
</p>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">informal</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> One who <a href = vnd.unilang:chats.html>chats</a> or talks to excess.
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2014</b> November 14,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blake_Bailey" class="extiw" title="w:Blake Bailey"><a href = vnd.unilang:blake.html>Blake</a> Bailey</a>,  “'Tennessee Williams,' by John Lahr  | print version: Theatrical victory of art <a href = vnd.unilang:over.html>over</a> life, <i>International New York Times</i>, 18 November 2014, p. 13 | ”, in  <cite><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_New_York_Times" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:The New York Times">The New York Times</a></cite> | <sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.nytimes.com/2014/11/16/books/review/tennessee-williams-by-john-lahr.html">[1]</a></sup>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">[S]he [Edwina, mother of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tennessee_Williams" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Tennessee Williams">Tennessee Williams</a>] <a href = vnd.unilang:was.html>was</a> indeed <a href = vnd.unilang:amanda.html>Amanda</a> [Wingfield, character in Williams' play <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Glass_Menagerie" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:The Glass Menagerie">The Glass <a href = vnd.unilang:menagerie.html>Menagerie</a></a></i>] in the flesh: a doughty <b><a href = vnd.unilang:chatterbox.html>chatterbox</a></b> from Ohio who adopted the manner of a Southern <a href = vnd.unilang:belle.html>belle</a> and eschewed both <a href = vnd.unilang:drink.html>drink</a> and sex to the greatest extent possible.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li>A cootie catcher <span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content qualifier-content">children's fortune-telling device</span><span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">)</span>.</li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">computing</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> <span class="form-of-definition use-with-mention">Synonym of <span class="form-of-definition-link"><i class="Latn mention" lang="en">chatterbot</i></span></span></li></ol>

</p>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Cheeseburger.jpg/220px-Cheeseburger.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Cheeseburger.jpg/330px-Cheeseburger.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Cheeseburger.jpg/440px-Cheeseburger.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2700" data-file-height="1800" />  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"></div>A <a href = vnd.unilang:cheeseburger.html>cheeseburger</a>.</div></div></div>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:cheeseburger.html>cheeseburger</a></strong> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en p-form-of" lang="en"><a href = vnd.unilang:cheeseburgers.html>cheeseburgers</a></b>)
</p>
<ol><li>A <a href = vnd.unilang:hamburger.html>hamburger</a> containing cheese (usually one or more <a href = vnd.unilang:slices.html>slices</a> of processed cheese).
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1956</b>,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frank_O%27Hara" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Frank O | Hara"><a href = vnd.unilang:frank.html>Frank</a> <a href = vnd.unilang:o.html>O</a>'<a href = vnd.unilang:hara.html>Hara</a></a>,  <cite>A Step Away from Them</cite> | <sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://www.poetryfoundation.org/poems/42662/a-step-away-from-them">[1]</a></sup>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">Neon in daylight <a href = vnd.unilang:is.html>is</a> a / great pleasure, as Edwin Denby would / write, as are light bulbs in daylight. / I <a href = vnd.unilang:stop.html>stop</a> for a <b><a href = vnd.unilang:cheeseburger.html>cheeseburger</a></b> at <a href = vnd.unilang:juliet.html>Juliet</a>'S / CORNER.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><b>2007</b>, Loretta Ichord, <i>Double <a href = vnd.unilang:cheeseburgers.html>Cheeseburgers</a>, <a href = vnd.unilang:quiche.html>Quiche</a>, and Vegetarian <a href = vnd.unilang:burritos.html>Burritos</a></i> (page 48)
<dl><dd>Busy Americans (many women <a href = vnd.unilang:were.html>were</a> working and not cooking as much) <a href = vnd.unilang:were.html>were</a> dining on foods such as deep-fried chicken, thick <a href = vnd.unilang:slices.html>slices</a> of <a href = vnd.unilang:pizza.html>pizza</a>, double <b><a href = vnd.unilang:cheeseburgers.html>cheeseburgers</a></b>, and big slabs of <a href = vnd.unilang:steak.html>steak</a>.</dd></dl></li></ul></li></ol>
